<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 18pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino; color: #ffffff; background-color: #808080;"><b><span style="line-height: 115%;">Spiritual Message for the Day â€“ Thatâ€™s Enough by Sri Swami Atmaswarupananda</span></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;">&nbsp;<strong style="text-indent: -0.5in;"><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times DigestÂ© | 15 September 2015 15.47 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span></strong></p>
<hr />
<div>
<table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" hspace="0" vspace="0" align="left">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td valign="top" align="left" style="padding-top: 0in; padding-right: 9.0pt; padding-bottom: 0in; padding-left: 9.0pt;">
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Thatâ€™s Enough<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Divine Life Society Publication: </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/messages/thatsenough.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Early Morning Meditation Talks</b></span></a></span><a name="_GoBack"></a><b> by Sri Swami Atmaswarupananda<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p align="center" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Om Sri Sadguru Paramatmane Namah<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Each religion, each philosophy has its own way of explaining life. But most seem to agree that in the beginning God alone was; then God created the world out of nothing or manifested Himself. They say that the One became the many; and yet, paradoxically, the One has never changed, even though the many appear to exist.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">If the One has never changed, the many must exist in our consciousness. And even here we have a strange phenomena. Because no matter what part of our consciousness we are experiencing, the other parts seem to be eternally there from the highest to the lowest. What we experience is where our attention is.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">According to Vedanta, there are two principal forces working on our attention. One is the force of <i>avidya maya</i>, which is constantly taking us into the many, and the second is the force of <i>vidya maya</i> which is constantly attracting us back to oneness. Why, when we are toldâ€”and it is trueâ€”that peace and happiness abide in oneness, are we attracted to the many, to separation? Perhaps it is because <i>avidya maya</i> constantly promises to satisfy all our desires, to make us someone special, even to make us like a god.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">These promises are named in all the scriptures as demoniacal promises. They are intoxicating promises, but they lead us to nothing except disasterâ€”to restlessness, to clash and quarrel. Even more, <i>avidya maya</i> never gives us the satisfaction that it promises. It promises to satisfy all our desires; instead it just adds fuel to the fire.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">So ultimately, with Godâ€™s grace, <i>vidya maya</i> has its opportunity. Through a <i>guru</i>, teaching or spiritual experience, we see the promise of a better way, the way of oneness. Thus to one degree or another, our lives turn around and we start heading in the homeward direction. But, <i>avidya maya</i> is still very much alive. And while it can no longer totally fool us, its tactic now becomes one of "thatâ€™s enough." We move a certain distance along with <i>vidya maya</i> and <i>avidya maya</i> says, "Thatâ€™s enough, you should be satisfied now." It does this at every step, and unfortunately, we frequently settle at a spiritual comfort level and get stuck there.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">But ultimately that level can never satisfy our souls. <i>Vidya maya</i> is ever calling us higher. This is why the <i>guru</i> will frequently disturb us, try to make us move higher. And if the <i>guru</i> doesnâ€™t do it, life will do it. Our wisdom knows that this is happening. Wisdom also recognises the nature of <i>avidya maya</i>, that even until the very end it never gives up the battle, that it is eternally thereâ€”its job being to drag us towards the many. But wisdom leads us to listen to <i>vidya maya</i>, which wants to take us back to the One.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">So as seekers, who are feeling the pull of <i>vidya maya</i>, feeling the pull of God, we must be aware that at all times <i>avidya maya</i> is sitting in waiting telling us, "Thatâ€™s enough. Youâ€™ve gone far enough. Be satisfied." But God, <i>guru</i> and <i>vidya maya</i> are telling us, "Itâ€™s never enough until you have reached the goal," and it is <i>vidya maya</i> we must always pay attention to.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt;"><span class="MsoHyperlink" style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Excerpts from:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;">&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Thatâ€™s Enough â€“ </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/messages/thatsenough.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Early Morning Meditation Talks</b></span></a></span></span><b><span style="font-size: 9.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> by Sri Swami Atmaswarupananda</span><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</div>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing"><span style="font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino; font-size: 12pt;">&nbsp;</span></p>
